Seven

Chapter Summary

Rio’s POV :)

Chapter Notes

In case yall were wondering - I garden, then I write this and hope it doesn’t wear off before I’m done with a chapter -

Here’s more slow burn - but don’t worry, it’ll get very heated, very soon :)

 

Rio didn’t get nervous. Not really. Not ever. 

 

She doesn’t let herself. 

 

And yet, standing next to Jen with her arm around her shoulders, she could feel something sharp and uncertain cutting through her usual confidence. 

 

The whole thing had been unexpected. She had been perfectly fine in the corner, thank you. 

 

It was entertaining watching the never-ending stream of photos play out in front of her. Everyone’s attentiveness towards the photographer dwindled more and more each time he clicked the shutter button. 

 

She definitely didn’t watch the kid and Agatha standing at the side - her hands on his shoulders, hanging onto every word he said as they waited for their turn. Their closeness was charming. Almost as if - 

 

But then Jen was turning towards Rio, and she heard the words, “I need one with my sister.” 

 

And Jen had said it like it was the simplest thing in the world. 

 

As if Evanora hadn’t specifically told Rio to stay out of the way unless she was called to help. Hell, Rio wasn’t even needed at the brunch, but Jen had put it on her schedule. And her contract said to follow the schedule. 

 

So she walked forward. Because Jen had asked for her. 

 

And then it was just the two of them in front of the camera, and Jen was leaning down, murmuring at best, “You don’t know who gave the kid makeup do you?” 

 

And Rio had to bite back a laugh. Because she saw Jen stick up for the kid to Evanora. She didn’t think Jen would put the pieces together. She normally doesn’t. “No idea.” 

 

And then the photographer was counting down. 

 

Rio and Jen both turned towards the photographer and Rio felt herself smile. 

 

Click. 

 

Then it was over. 

 

And Evanora was directing everyone back to their seats, and Jen was pulled to the side and Rio was at the back of the crowd. 

 

So she waited until everyone had found their seats, definitely not keeping an eye on where someone specific was sitting.

 

And she definitely didn’t choose a table by herself specifically on the other side of the room from that specific person. 

 

Just when she had settled back into her seat, she felt the table shift and someone sliding into the seat next to her. 

 

Billy. 

 

Rio turned towards him, watching as he scooted his chair closer, arms crossed over his chest. He was looking at her like he was trying to solve a puzzle, or she was the puzzle. 

 

“So.” He said after a long moment. 

 

Rio raised her eyebrow at him, saying nothing. 

 

“What are you doing here?” 

 

Rio blinked, “At brunch?” 

 

“At the wedding,” he clarified. “I’ve never met you before, and yet my Aunt Jen is asking for a photo with you,” he drew out. “Her sister.”

 

Rio shook her head, “I’m the florist.” 

 

“Jen’s sister.” 

 

Well. 

 

He’s not going to drop this. Rio was already way past her limits of feeling off today. She wasn’t going to be explaining her relationship to Agatha’s son. 

 

Rio hasn’t even let herself address that - because she’s pretty sure Billy is a teenager. And if Rio counted the years she’s been gone from Westview - nope that hasn’t changed in the last 48 hours - that’s still only eight years. 

 

Rio would’ve remembered if Agatha had been pregnant. Because they would’ve been kids. 

 

Billy was still looking at her, looking for any kind of clue. 

 

So no - Rio was not addressing the sister comment, the Aunt Jen comment, or the fact that Billy is probably Agatha’s son, somehow. Not that it’s Rio’s business. 

 

“You go to Westview High, right?” she asked. That seemed to do it, as it looked like Billy was thrown off by the sudden shift in topic. 

 

“.. Yeah?” 

 

“Mrs. Hart still teaching English?” 

 

That got a groan out of him, Rio smirked. 

 

“It’s Mrs. Davis now.” 

 

Rio gave herself a pat on the back, because everyone dreaded her class. She was the nicest lady until she was grading your assignments. But Rio always could get through to her, because one day she found out Mrs. Hart loved to garden. 

 

So maybe Rio used her plant knowledge during high school to get on the teacher’s good side. At least that time, she wasn’t using it as a line to get into a girl’s pants. 

 

“You know, she doesn’t tell anyone this, but she’s a big gardener. Want some plant facts to get her off your back?” 

 

Billy was grinning, leaning in, “You’d really do that?” 

 

And Rio was nodding along. Because plant facts - she could do plant facts right now. 

 

And then there was a banging sound over the speakers in the dining hall, and as Rio looked up, Evanora was standing at a podium at the front of the dining hall, tapping her finger on the microphone in front of her. 

 

Then Evanora was speaking, and Rio had mostly pushed that out of her mind. 

 

Mostly. 

 

She told herself not to listen to Evanora. She really did. 

 

Because whatever was going to come out of her mouth was going to probably sting at Rio a little bit. 

 

And she was right. 

 

“I’ve never been prouder of my daughter,” she said, and the words were light, effortless. “She has grown into such a smart, talented woman, and I couldn’t ask for a better person to take on the family’s legacy.” 

 

Rio stared back down at the tablecloth. 

 

Evanora was still speaking. 

 

But she couldn’t hear her anymore, not if she tried. 

 

It wasn’t like she hadn’t heard it all before. She had. In different forms, different ways over the years. 

 

It just is different to hear it in public, in front of other people. 

 

Because her dad died. And she was left with Evanora. 

 

Evanora never let her forget that. 

 

So Rio knew this. 

 

Rio knew Jen was taking on Evanora’s business at some point. 

 

Because it was her family’s legacy - and Rio, well, Rio was left with Evanora. Because her dad married Evanora, and then died.

 

But dammit - it’s hard to hear in public. With other people clapping along. 

 

It was so stupid to even let it get to her, after all these years. Maybe she should’ve been over it by now. Maybe she was over it. Maybe the bottomless mimosas were getting to her. 

 

But she wasn’t sticking around to hear the rest of it. 

 

And so Rio stood up, and walked out of the room. She felt eyes on her as she left, but she didn’t bother to look back. She’s sure half the dining room watched her walk out the door. 

 

She couldn’t breathe. 

 

Her feet carried her forward, past the venue, past the parked cars, until she reached her van. Keys in hand. 

 

Then she realized she definitely cannot drive right now - not like this. Mimosas or not, her vision was tunneled and oh, her hands were shaking. She could hear the keys jangling somewhere down on her near her left side. 

 

Taking a look at her surroundings, she could go left towards the edge of town, or take a right and head towards main street. 

 

Her feet directed her automatically. 

 

Rio was trying to count her steps and center herself, she felt her lips in an ‘o’ shape as she was exhaling.


Damn, was she breathing that loud? 

 

Suddenly she was in front of shops on the main road, and they were all unfamiliar. A coffee shop that wasn’t there when she was in high school. And a record store? Was Westview even big enough to support a record store? 

 

Finally - she was standing in front of Calderu’s Books. 

 

She hadn’t been here in - well Rio’s covered this already - eight years. But the sight of it still felt the same - warm, welcoming, like it had been waiting for her. 

 

She stepped inside, hearing the bell above the door jingle as it always did, and the scent of paper and coffee wrapped around her. Rio still hadn’t thought about where she was going as she turned and walked towards the corner - her corner - where, thank God, her chair was still there. 

 

It’s not really her chair - but Lilia used to let her read in it, undisturbed until Evanora’s curfew. 

 

She ran her fingers along the back of it, feeling the fray of the fabric. A well loved chair. Cherished. 

 

The sound of someone walking up behind her pulled Rio out of her thoughts, “Well, well. If it isn’t Rio Vidal.” 

 

And Rio turned and looked at Lilia, and she felt her mouth lifting into a second genuine smile today. 

 

“You’re still here.” 

 

Lilia laughed. “And you’re back. Come on, I have some coffee over at the counter.” 

 

Lilia was already turning around, knowing Rio would follow her. And she did. 

 

Lilia went behind the counter while Rio sat at a bar stool next to the register. She thinks it's the first time she’s sat in one of these bar stools even though she’s visited the store hundreds of times. 

 

Then Lilia was asking Rio what she did now, and Rio told her about her shop. Then she was asking her about how it was living in New York, and Rio was answering. She never once asked her what she was doing in Westview - but she must’ve known - everyone knew everything about everyone in Westview. Finally, Lilia ran out of questions, but Rio didn’t want the conversation to be over, so Rio asked about the bookstore. 

 

Lilia’s lips quirked, “I don’t run the place anymore, so I wouldn’t know.” 

 

Rio frowned slightly, “What do you mean?” 

 

Because it sure looked like Lilia ran the place.

None of the decorations had changed, Rio’s chair was still in the corner, the sign still said Calderu’s Books, hell Lilia was behind the counter. 

 

And Lilia just laughed. All-knowing like. 

 

Rio didn’t like that. 

 

But the bell at the front of the shop rang, and Lilia was smiling at the customers that just walked in and - 

 

Of course. 

 

Rio should’ve known. Because for an hour, she hadn’t thought about Agatha. And the universe must have thought that was too long. 

 

Because Agatha was standing at the front of the door with Billy at her side, and she was pulling off her sunglasses and throwing her purse on the counter, walking in like she owned the place. She hadn’t noticed Rio, yet. 

 

“Thank you for watching the counter. I know you’re doing it more later this week for the wedding, but I can’t thank -” Agatha looked towards the counter then. 

 

With Rio sitting across from Lilia. 

 

Rio didn’t have to look to see Lilia grinning. She could feel it from where she sat. 

 

And Billy - Billy was grinning ear to ear. “Rio!”

 

But Lilia was already grabbing at Billy’s shoulder, “Hey kid, I’m glad you’re here. I need you to help me bring in a few boxes from the delivery this morning.” 

 

And then it was just Rio and Agatha. Wait what? How did this happen so fast? 

 

Rio was still in her bar stool, staring at Agatha, who was staring right back. 

 

And if it was any other day, literally any other day, Rio would love this. She’d take her time with it, stretch it out, play whatever game to keep Agatha’s attention. 

 

But she really did not have it in her right now. Not after Jen pulled her into a photo because she needed one with her sister. Not after Evanora’s speech about the family legacy. Not after finding out Lilia doesn’t run her bookstore anymore. 

 

But Rio was also pretty quick - and Agatha was stepping behind the counter. 

 

So Lilia gave the bookstore to Agatha. Or sold it to her. Or something. Because Lilia said she didn’t run it anymore and there she was standing behind the counter. 

 

Agatha. 

 

Then she was talking to Rio, “You know, I had this whole plan to not engage with you today. Or for the rest of the wedding.” 

 

That was definitely not what Rio was expecting to hear. 

 

“Yet, here you are. Again. I can’t seem to escape you,” Agatha finished. 

 

“Here I am.” Rio replied, looking into Agatha’s eyes finally. 

 

Agatha’s eyebrows furrowed, like she was concerned or - something. Rio’s not sure. 

 

Does Rio look that pitiful right now? This is why she came to the bookstore - to hide in her corner - to be away from other gazes, other people. 

 

Then there was silence again, both not breaking eye contact. 

 

She didn’t mean to - but Rio broke first this time. Looking at the menu just behind Agatha’s head. 

 

Then Agatha was turning around, and grabbed a mug off the shelf, helping herself to some of the coffee behind the counter. And then she was turning back towards Rio again, taking a slow slip from her now full mug. 

 

“So.” 

 

Rio arched an eyebrow, “So?” 

 

“Have you met Ralph yet?” Agatha chose to ask. 

 

And Rio really didn’t expect that either. It’s like she couldn’t figure out Agatha’s next move, no matter how hard she tried. Because why did she ask that?

 

“Haven’t had the pleasure,” she heard herself respond. 

 

“Oh, pleasure is not the right word if you actually knew him.” Agatha responded. 

 

And maybe Rio was wrong - maybe she did have it in her. Or maybe it was just because her and Agatha were alone again. Rio’s not sure. 

 

“If I recall, last night you said the same nice things about him.” 

 

Agatha’s eyes snapped to hers quickly, “Let’s not talk about last night.” 

 

Rio dramatically looked around the room, “Seems like now is as good as any.” 

 

“I didn’t -” Agatha stopped herself. She started again, “I thought -” she stopped. Again. 

 

Yeah - Rio definitely did have it in her still, despite the emotional rollercoaster this morning. 

 

“You thought that I was someone else?” 

 

Agatha took a harsh sip out of her mug, “And you knew exactly who I was.” 

 

Her words were sharp - like Agatha was holding onto them since last night. And she was looking into Rio’s eyes so unwavering, Rio had to look away - again. 

 

Twice. In like two minutes. 

 

“I did.” Rio said. 

 

Then she was looking at Agatha again, “So you just let me, what? Make a fool of myself?” 

 

Rio frowned, “Fool?” she said, not believing Agatha just said that. “You didn’t make a fool of yourself.” Rio’s head was shaking back and forth in disbelief. 

 

Is that really how Agatha felt about their… conversation last night? 

 

Agatha was nodding her head, and she looked like she was about to respond. So Rio beat her to it. 

 

“Would you really have kept talking to me if you knew who I was?” 

 

Checkmate. 

 

Because Agatha’s lips were pressed in a line. 

 

“It’s okay, Agatha. I know you wouldn’t have continued if you knew.” 

 

“You’re twisting it around.” 

 

Rio was leaning forward now, “Am I, though?” 

 

Agatha didn’t respond. She finished her cup of coffee, though, and turned towards the sink behind the counter. She started washing the cup, so Rio continued. 

 

“That’s why I never told you.”

 

Agatha turned back around, the coffee mug being dried off with a towel now in her hands. She kept their eye contact as she finished drying it off, not even glancing towards her hands as she put the mug back on the shelf. 

 

“I know I said it before, but thank you for what you did for Billy earlier today.” 

 

Rio should’ve known she’d changed the subject. But Agatha keeps surprising her. Ever since she showed up in Westview, Agatha makes moves Rio cannot predict no matter how hard she tries. 

 

“How mad was Evanora?” she heard herself asking Agatha. 

 

“Honestly? I don’t know. I try my best to avoid her at any event. But if I had to guess on a scale of one to ten? Sixteen.” Agatha said with a straight face. 

 

Rio laughed. She sure loved when Evanora’s world burned in front of her. 

 

And Rio could see it - Agatha’s lips twitching like she was fighting a smile.

 

The bell over the door rang again, and Billy was walking in, out of breath. Lilia followed behind him, brushing dust off her sleeves. 

 

“I really do love having a big, strong grandson,” Lilia said as she ruffled Billy’s hair. Billy squirmed under her touch but smiled nonetheless. And Agatha was looking at them both with an effortless smile. 

 

But for Rio? The dots were finally connecting. Because Billy was for sure Agatha’s. And that meant Agatha was Lilia’s. 

 

How Rio grew up in this bookstore and never realized Agatha was Lilia’s daughter was beyond her. But then again - Lilia never really talked to Rio when she was in the store growing up. She just let her be. And it’s not like Rio or Agatha talked before, well, now. 

 

Rio felt herself standing up out of her barstool, and was reaching into her wallet to buy the coffee.

 

Agatha was shaking her head, “Don’t worry about it.” 

 

Then she was grabbing the cup from the counter, washing it the same way she just washed hers. 

 

“Are you going to the spa thing tomorrow?” 

 

Rio blinked, “The what?” 

 

Agatha turned and gave her a look, “The wedding party spa trip. In Eastview. The one Jen wants us all at?” 

 

And Rio was back in reality. In Westview. Talking to her stepsister’s best friend. 

 

“I know better than to miss it,” she responded, slipping both hands into her pants pockets. 

 

Agatha nodded, “Okay.” That’s all Rio got from her. 

 

But then Lilia was stepping in front of Rio, rubbing up and down Rio’s arms, as if she’s always done that to Rio, “You should stop by more often.” 

 

Rio really did not have a response to that, so she offered her trademark smirk, turned towards Billy and nodded at him and then was walking towards the door. 

 

She didn’t need to turn around to know Agatha was watching her leave.

 

She could feel it. 

Eight

Chapter Summary

So I was definitely full gardened writing this - still am - but right now I think it makes sense so it's getting posted :)

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The door has barely shut behind Rio before Agatha let out a slow breath, pressing her hands into the cool counter to ground herself. She was not going to let this interaction between her and Rio consume her thoughts. 

 

She turned and saw the stacks of boxes Billy must have brought in earlier while she and Rio were talking. Well - she definitely could go for some shelf stocking right now. Maybe if Billy helped her, she could keep the conversation going and avoid thinking about - 

 

“I wanna go to the movies,” Billy announced, climbing onto one of the bar stools near the register. 

 

Because of course he does. And of course he’s going to announce it while Lilia is here, she loves the movies. Agatha was pretty sure Billy had caught on that Lilia would take him to the movies to get out of chores, as long as he asked her in front of Agatha.

 

Agatha raised an eyebrow, “Oh do you now? This wouldn’t have to do with all the books I need help stocking, does it?”

 

Lilia was stepping in before Billy had a chance to respond, “Now, I never made you stock the shelves while you were under my roof. He shouldn’t have to, either.” 

 

Dammit. 

 

Lilia was right. 

 

When Lilia had adopted Agatha, she never enforced many rules. Curfew was before Lilia went to sleep - sometimes eleven, sometimes two. She never had to check in, as long as she stuck with Jen and Alice. Agatha definitely did not have to help out in the shop, which was really unfortunate for current Agatha right now, who wanted someone there with her as a distraction. 

 

But, Lilia had always trusted Agatha. 

 

Agatha promised herself when she and Wanda had officially become Billy’s guardians, she would give him the same trust Lilia had given her.

 

“Fine, you’re right. Go, both of you. Enjoy the movie. Bring back some popcorn if you have any left.” Agatha said. 

 

Billy’s smile was ear-to-ear as he literally dragged Lilia out of the front door with him. 

 

Lilia was laughing as she was pulled along. “We’ll be back later.”

 

So Agatha did the only thing she knew how to do now that she was alone again: stocking. 

 

Unfortunately for her, it did nothing except to stop her from replaying her conversation with Rio. 

 

You didn’t make a fool of yourself. 

 

Agatha rolled her eyes at the memory.


What did that even mean? 

 

Was Rio actually into the flirting? 

 

Or was she just playing along - because that’s what Rio did. Because Rio played along with things, let the mess happen then moved on without a second thought. 

 

Except, Rio did care. She had to. 

 

The makeup for Billy and now running out of the brunch after - was it Evanora that was speaking when she left? Yeah, it must have been because Agatha wasn’t listening to it. 

 

But then why did Rio come here? To her bookstore? 

 

Instead of her hotel? Or wherever she was staying. Not that Agatha has thought about it.  

 

Rio obviously hadn’t known the store was Agatha’s now. Agatha remembered the surprise on her face when she walked behind the counter. 

 

But she also remembers how easily Rio had spoken with Lilia. They had been talking for a while, judging by how comfortably Rio had been leaning on the counter - 

 

Agatha shook her head and turned back towards the nearest shelf, adjusting a few of the books. 

 

She shouldn’t even be thinking about this. About her. 

 

Because Rio was Jen’s step-sister. 

 

Or sister. 

 

Isn’t that what Jen called her today when she asked for photos with her? 

 

Jen surprised Agatha twice today. In the span of an hour, stood up to her mother in defense of Billy and specifically asked for a photo with Rio. 

 

Her sister. 

 

The bell at the front of the store ran out and she nearly jumped at the sound. Customers. A perfect distraction. 

 

She put on her polite customer service smile as she turned towards the entrance, greeting the couple who walked in. Agatha was even mentally patting herself on her back because she hadn’t thought about Rio the entire time she walked the couple through the aisles of bookshelves. 

 

Until checkout. 

 

At the register. 

 

Right where Rio had been sitting earlier today. In her brunch outfit. Leaning over the counter. 

 

It took everything in Agatha to go back to the stack of boxes once her customers had left. But she needed to do it. Distract herself. 

 

By the time Lilia and Billy returned from their movie, Agatha had emptied five of the boxes. Only five. 

 

But then Billy was telling her about the film, and that snapped her out of her thoughts real quick, because she was definitely following along. To the storyline of the movie they just went to see - Spiderboy? - yeah that one. 

 

Then Billy excused himself to the restroom, and Agatha felt Lilia’s eyes on her. 

 

She turned to see Lilia watching her with a gleeful look. 

 

She felt her eyes narrow. “How do you know Rio?”

 

Lilia’s eyebrows rose, “It’s Westview, Agatha.” 

 

Agatha scoffed, “It just seemed like you guys have known each other more than just in passing, is all.”

“I tried everything, Rio. You blocked me and ran and never once reached out. You ran from me at the bleachers and you’ve been running ever since.”

And what the actual fuck is Wanda on?

Anger starts in her stomach. Hot. Acidic. It rises fast, crawling into her chest and up her throat. Because—no. No. No.

She chased Wanda. Everywhere. Hid behind dumpsters and ducked behind library shelves just to steal a few kisses after school. Spent senior year tangled in lies just to get scraps of affection. They had a plan. They had a fucking plan.

And then—right before graduation—Wanda dropped the bomb. Her and Vision had to be together. She was going to follow her parents’ bullshit blueprint. No warning. No chance to even fight for her.

Rio had said okay. Okay, fine. If that’s what you want.

And then she left.

Heart shattered but shoulders back. Took the damn plan and ran with it. Opened her shop. Built her life. Alone, yeah but free. In New York. Making art. Meeting women. On her own terms.

She was fine.

She is fine.

And then—fuck.

Agatha.

Her brain slams into the name like a wall.

Not just Agatha. Dinner.

“Shit,” Rio mutters aloud. She shoots to her feet, looking around frantically for her phone. “What time is it?”

Fuck.

Rio snatches her phone off the desk, heart pounding against her ribs like it’s trying to escape her chest. The lock screen’s lit up—missed calls, unread messages.

Because of course she’s late. Of course.

She’s about thirty minutes late.

Fuck. 

Agatha.

She doesn’t even read them. She can’t. Not while Wanda’s still sitting ten feet away, spinning her own version of the past like it was some kind of tragic love story instead of the worst goddamn heartbreak of Rio’s life.

So she just types.

Rio:

something came up. I’ll be there tomorrow for whatever is on the itinerary. sorry.

Not a good message. Not even close. But it’s fast. Clean. Enough to stop them from waiting on her, enough to buy her time to fucking breathe. She’ll send a better message later. Fix it. Make it up to Agatha somehow. 

Right now?

Wanda.

Wanda with her hands clasped in her lap like she’s the one who got hurt. Wanda, watching her with that same unreadable, wide-eyed look that always made Rio feel like she was being studied. Picked apart.

“Really?” Wanda scoffs. “I just tell you all of that and you’re on your phone?”

Rio turns to her sharply, eyes flashing. “Hold on a fucking second. I had dinner plans.”

“Whatever,” Wanda huffs. Like it’s nothing.

Rio feels her jaw tighten again. “What do you want me to say, Wanda?”

“I don’t know. Something. Anything!”

Rio can’t help it, she laughs. It’s bitter. Ugly. “I don’t see why it’s such a big deal anymore now, Wanda. You told me you weren’t going through with our plans the day before we were going to leave. Are you really mad that my eighteen-year-old self blocked you?”

Her phone buzzes in her palm again.

She ignores it. Her voice gets louder.

“Wanda, you broke my heart that day. It was supposed to be us against the world. I lost myself trying to love you. Chasing you down like some secret. Whatever you wanted, I’d kill myself trying to get it for you.”

Wanda flinches. Rio doesn’t stop.

“And the day before graduation, you tell me never mind, you’re going to start dating some dude? Vision? You think that didn’t gut me?”

“But I didn’t!” Wanda blurts, voice pitching high. “You’re not listening, Rio, I tried. I tried to tell you—”

“But you were going to go through with it at first,” Rio snaps, eyes hot now, throat tight. “Even if you changed your mind. I wasn’t the first choice then.”

Wanda’s expression breaks, just for a second. And Rio - 

She can’t stand it.

Because she used to dream about that face. 

And all she wants is to go back thirty minutes and get to dinner on time. To Agatha.

Instead, she’s here. Stuck with a ghost from her own past. 

“That’s not fair, Rio. I was also just a kid. Going against my parents’ wishes? I did it. And you still left.”

Rio doesn’t even blink. Doesn’t flinch. She’s so far past done with this conversation, she might as well be in another fucking dimension. “Wanda, this is all in the past. Why does it matter anymore?”

It comes out sharper than she planned, but good. Maybe it’ll cut through whatever version of reality Wanda’s clinging to.

“Honestly?” Wanda says, soft, almost like she’s trying to sound wounded. “I told you earlier. I wanted to see you for myself. I never thought I’d see you in Westview again.”

Yeah, well. She never thought she’d be here either. If it wasn’t for this wedding, she’d still be in New York, blissfully Wanda-free.

“Well,” Rio says, arms crossed tight over her chest, “you saw me.”

And Wanda—fucking giggles. 

What the fuck. 

Like this is a reunion. Like this is funny. Like any of this is okay.

It makes Rio want to scream.

Instead, she starts moving toward the door. No words. No warning. She just wants her out. Now. She grabs the handle and gestures—not kindly.

Wanda doesn’t budge.

“Wait. Wait, Rio. Wait.”

So Rio does. Not because she wants to. Because something in her spine tells her to hold still. And they’re too close now. Wanda’s standing in her space like she’s still welcome in it. Like nothing ever happened. Like she still knows her.

She doesn’t.

Rio just wants her gone. She can’t breathe right, the air in the room too thick, too tight.

Then—she feels it. A hand on her arm.

And that’s when Rio shuts down.

Rio shuts her eyes.

Wanda’s hand is still on her arm, fingers curled in a way that sends ice crawling down her spine. It doesn’t feel warm. Doesn’t feel familiar. It feels wrong.

She wants it off. Now.

She goes to push it away, gentle at first—just enough pressure to say don’t—but Wanda’s grip tightens. Stronger than expected. Possessive. 

“These are new,” Wanda says, voice low. Fingertips brushing over the ink on Rio’s forearm. 

And—fuck. Is she really asking about her tattoos right now?

Rio yanks her arm back. “Wanda, I think you should go.”

It’s not a question. It’s barely polite.

Wanda nods. Like she agrees. 

But she doesn’t fucking move.

Rio turns away. One step toward the door. Her heart is hammering in her throat. Every inch of her skin feels like it’s vibrating with pressure. She can’t breathe. Can’t think—

And then—

Another knock.

Another knock.

Rio is one second away from throwing her phone, her chair, maybe herself out the damn window.

Who the fuck else needs something from her tonight?

She moves fast. Doesn’t think. Just yanks the door open because maybe - maybe, whoever it is can help her get Wanda the hell out of her room. 

And of course. 

Of fucking course.

Everything gets so much worse.

Eighteen

Chapter Summary

Rio’s POV (Part 2)

**please read the author’s note at the bottom**

Chapter Notes

So I took this four different directions before I was okay with this direction.
Hope yall enjoy! I’m still gardened in case you were wondering 😎
Also ! I posted another chapter earlier today you may want to read that first before reading this chapter it will not make sense even kind of :)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

It’s Jen.

She doesn’t look past the threshold. Doesn’t glance into the room. Doesn’t check for a reaction, or if she’s interrupting something, or even if Rio is alone.

She just talks. Like she memorized every word. Like she’s rehearsed it over and over in her head on the way down the hall and now she’s scared to deviate. Scared of whatever the answer might be.

“Hey, uh—Agatha said something came up for dinner,” Jen says, fast. Stiff. “And I just wanted to make sure it wasn’t something I did. Or that any of us did. Because, Rio, I know we weren’t ever close growing up but—Wanda?”

And fuck.

It’s worse.

Somehow. Instantly. Unquestionably.

Worse.

Rio doesn’t even know why yet. Can’t name it. Can’t pin it down. But the second Jen says that name, it’s like something in her chest lurches sideways.

Wanda is behind her. Still.

Silent.

Not helping.

Probably smirking.

Rio doesn’t have to turn around to know it. Can feel the smugness radiating off her like heat.

Jen doesn’t know about them. Never did. Neither did Evanora. No one. Not a soul. That was the point. That was the rule. It had been theirs—just theirs. A secret folded tight between lockers and gym bleachers and the backs of movie theaters. The kind of secret sealed in whispered promises and shaky hands under a blanket of stars.

Well—Pietro knew.

Once.

Senior year. He walked in on them kissing in Wanda’s bedroom. Blinked like he didn’t quite register it, then yelled, “Use protection!” in the voice of a sitcom dad and shut the door behind him like it never happened.

Rio hadn’t thought about that night in years. Another memory she boxed up and shoved to the back of her brain. Padlocked it. Buried it. Along with every Wanda-shaped feeling she swore she was done with.

Until now.

Until this week.

Now everything’s pressing in. Tight and sharp and too loud. Her chest feels like it’s wrapped in wire. Her hands are cold. Her brain won’t stay still.

She should’ve said no to Evanora.

Should’ve said no to this wedding. To Westview. To this whole damn week.

Her life is supposed to be calm now. She built it that way. Carefully. Intentionally. Piece by piece. Flower by flower. Client by client. No drama. No mess. No history.

Nothing like this.

Jen is still there. Still blinking at her. Still waiting.

Still expecting her to say something that makes sense.

“Hey Jen. Long time no see, like at least 20 minutes” Wanda says, casual as hell.

Rio doesn’t turn around. Doesn’t need to.

She hears the shift in Jen’s voice immediately. A full stop. Sharpened.

“Why are you here?” Jen asks.

And Wanda? Doesn’t miss a beat. “Why are you here?”

Her tone matches. Just as biting. Just as loaded.

And Rio—

Rio hasn’t said anything real yet. Not a single word that matters. Her throat is too thick, too locked up, and her brain won’t stop spiraling. Everything feels like it’s moving too fast and too slow all at once.

She’s going to lose it. Right here. In front of both of them.

Freak out. Snap. Scream.

Or maybe all three.

“I was just checking on Rio,” Jen says again. Rewinds. Replays. Her voice softens slightly, like it’s an afterthought. “Am I interrupting something?”

“No!” Rio blurts. Too loud. Too fast. “No, you’re not.”

It sounds like a lie.

Because it is. Rio’s brain just hasn’t caught up to what exactly Jen’s interrupting. 

And the interruption is very much welcomed. 

Wanda scoffs. Crosses the room without hesitation. Like she owns the place. Like she’s not the one who lit this whole thing on fire in the first place.

She pulls a sleek little business card from her jacket pocket. Holds it out like it’s a peace offering. 

“Just… text me before you go back to New York, okay?” she says. “We can get coffee or something.”

Rio nods.

She doesn’t mean to. Doesn’t even think about it. It’s reflex. An escape hatch.

She just needs her gone.

Jen watches the whole exchange with her head tilted slightly. Eyes narrowed. Quiet.

She doesn’t say a word until the door shuts behind Wanda.

Then she shakes her head. Slow. Like she just watched something derail in real time.

“What was that?” she asks, low. Not angry. Not yet. Just confused. Baffled. Like she’s trying to do math in her head and nothing’s adding up.

Rio feels the panic rising again. Crawling up her spine. Throat tight. Every muscle braced. 

She clears her throat. 

“I guess Billy told her about the makeup I gave him at brunch the other day,” Rio muttered, barely keeping her voice steady. “She figured out I was in town and showed up. Said she wanted to talk.”

Jen leaned against the doorframe, arms crossed. Not angry. Not even skeptical. Just… watching.

Observing in that quiet, unnerving way she always had. The way that made Rio feel like she was being held under a microscope, whether she wanted to be or not. Evanora does the same thing. Rio tries not to think about that either. 

Rio rubbed a hand down her face. “You honestly just saved me. I’ve been trying to get her to leave for—God. Forever.”

But Jen doesn’t move. Doesn’t speak. Still just staring like she’s waiting for something more. Like she already knows the outline and is giving Rio a chance to fill in the details herself. No pressure. Just enough silence to dig into her skin.

And then Jen lets out a quiet laugh. There’s a beat, and then,  “I didn’t know who gave Billy the makeup. Agatha swore it wasn’t her. Honestly, Alice told me it wasn’t her, but I didn’t believe her.” She shakes her head slightly. “Can’t believe I didn’t put it together that it was yours.”

That makes Rio glance up. Just for a second.

Jen’s expression is somewhere between amused and stunned. 

Jen tilts her head. “What did Wanda want to talk about?”

And there it is.

Rio had been hoping—naively—that Jen might let that part go. Might not ask. Might pretend she didn’t walk in on what she walked in on.

But of course not.

That’s not how Jen works. And that’s not how this week is going. Every moment seems designed to drag up something Rio thought she buried years ago.

She sighs. Long and low. Her voice barely above a whisper. “Honestly? I don’t know. We… we were together for like six months senior year. But we broke it off just before graduation.”

The words feel heavier than she expected. She doesn’t look at Jen while she says them. Just stares at her shoes like they might help hold her together. Like the admission might hurt less if she doesn’t meet anyone’s eyes while she says it.

Jen doesn’t respond.

Not right away.

And that somehow feels worse than any reaction Rio had braced herself for. Worse than judgment. Worse than confusion.

So she keeps talking. Too fast. Filling the silence before it can turn on her.

“It was high school. It wasn’t—serious or anything. She probably just… I don’t know. Wanted closure. Or to check in. Or something.”

She’s rambling now. Can hear it in her own voice. The pitch. The pace.

Because the truth is—she doesn’t know what Wanda wanted.

She hasn’t even let herself figure out how she feels about any of it. Not yet. Not when it all hit so fast. Not when it’s been sealed in the back of her mind for so long it barely felt real until today.

Jen’s eyes narrow. Her arms stay crossed. And she stares at Rio like she’s scanning for fine print. Like she’s trying to find the one sentence that doesn’t match the rest of the story.

“Nothing happened?”

The question lands soft.

Too soft.

And it makes Rio flinch a little, because it sounds harmless, but it isn’t. Not really. 

But Rio doesn’t lie.

Not about this.

“No—God, no. It’s over. Been over.” Her voice comes out sharper now. More certain. Like she’s trying to ground herself with the truth. Like saying it more forcefully might make it feel more final. “I honestly was hoping I’d luck out and not see her this entire trip.”

And she means that.

She means it so much she can feel the panic still humming under her skin. Still trying to claw its way out. She doesn’t want to give Wanda another second in her brain.

So before Jen can say another word—before she can even look at her with that careful, reading-too-much-into-it expression—Rio grabs the business card still clutched in her hand, tears it clean down the middle, and throws it straight into the trash.

Not for show.

Well—maybe a little for show.

But mostly for herself.

She’s not calling Wanda. She’s not texting her. She’s not grabbing coffee. She’s not reopening that box.

She’s not.

Jen watches her for another beat, eyes steady. Still measuring. Still calculating something behind that quiet gaze.

Then, finally, she shrugs. “Fine. But since I just saved you—you’re welcome, by the way—you can make it up to me by coming to dinner.” Her smile softens. “We waited for you.”

And Jesus. Fuck. 

Rio feels it like a punch.

Not from Jen’s words—but from what’s underneath them.

They waited for her.

That shouldn’t hit her as hard as it does. Shouldn’t knock the wind out of her like it matters. But something inside her—something tight and protective and half-frozen since she got to Westview—sits up a little straighter at the sound of it.

She swallows around the lump building in her throat.

Grabs her phone.

Falls into step behind Jen without a word, sliding into the car like her body knows what to do even if her brain’s still catching up.

The silence in the car is merciful. Calm. Jen doesn’t push, doesn’t prod. Just drives, one hand on the wheel, the other drumming lightly on her thigh. It’s easy. Comfortable. Like none of the last ten minutes between the two of them happened. Like Rio isn’t still trying to claw her way out of whatever the hell that moment with Wanda was.

Eventually, Rio unlocks her phone.

Notifications flare to life—missed calls, a few texts.

Alice. Jen. But it’s Agatha’s name that catches her thumb. That makes her breath catch in her chest.

She opens their thread.

Agatha

hey we made it to the restaurant we’re headed in :)

we got a corner booth :)

jen ordered you a drink - it’s a joke (i think)

[a photo of a drink with - Rio has to squint at the picture - a gummy penis hanging off the rim]

okay I’m now drinking ur penis drink

 

Rio stares at the messages, her screen glowing in the dim car. Her heart stutters once, then settles into a low, uneasy thrum. She scrolls down.

 

Her own last text:

Rio

something came up. I’ll be there tomorrow for whatever is on the itinerary. sorry.

 

And right below it:

Agatha

okay! I hope everything’s ok - I’ll tell jen.

not to be too horny but does that mean no to your hotel room tonight (i blame your penis drink)

 

Rio presses the back of the phone to her lips, lets her eyes close for just a second.

She feels herself smile. Just a little bit. Not sure how a gummy penis drink is making her smile. 

Rio knows it’s not the drink. 

When they pull up outside the restaurant, Rio hesitates just outside the door.

Through the window, she can already see the table. Billy’s mid-story, eyes wide, hands flying. Alice is leaned in close beside him, clearly egging him on, grinning. 

Across from them, Agatha. Elbow on the table, chin resting in her palm, smiling at whatever Billy’s saying. She laughs, then—real and open and unbothered—and it hits Rio square in the chest.

Hard.

She doesn’t know why she feels like this. Not exactly.

Maybe it’s Wanda. Maybe it’s Agatha. Maybe it’s both of them crashing together in her brain.

Or maybe it’s the fact that Billy’s sitting right there. 

It’s Jen’s turn to surprise Rio.

Just as they walk up to the table, Jen claps a hand on Rio’s back—firm, grounding, almost proud.

“I come bearing Rio,” she announces, all charm and no edge. “You’re welcome, by the way. We couldn’t get her van to start.”

Her van?

Rio nearly stares at her. That’s the story? She almost wants to laugh, but the way Jen says it—so smooth, so offhanded—makes it impossible to argue. Like there’s nothing suspicious about any of it.

Alice, thank God, doesn’t question it. Just groans. “Thank God it broke down here and not in Eastview. You’d have had to wait six hours for a tow.”

And Agatha—Agatha finally looks up. “Mmhm.”

Rio’s breath catches hard in her throat.

Because Agatha looks at her. Really looks. Not just a glance or a polite acknowledgment—but a slow, deliberate sweep of her eyes that lingers just a second too long.

She’s in a simple button-up and slacks, nothing flashy, nothing meant to draw attention. But the glasses—Jesus—the glasses are different from earlier.

Rounder frames. Dark tortoiseshell. A little crooked on her face like she’s been pushing them up and down without thinking, the bridge smudged from her thumb. It makes her look a little disheveled. 

Rio wants to ruin her.

“Yes, yes, thank you, Jen, for saving me,” she says quickly, her voice pitched just a little too high, the words tripping out fast as she tries not to look like she’s staring. She tugs out the only open chair—right next to Agatha—and sits before her legs can change their mind.

Jen drops into the empty seat beside Billy, her job done, ordering a drink for Rio - commenting that she’d drive everyone home.

Rio’s still trying to get a handle on her own pulse, still focused on not combusting, when she feels it.

A finger.

Light. Deliberate. Pressing just above her knee.

The air stutters out of her lungs.

Just one touch—but it’s confident. Possessive.

Like Agatha didn’t even think twice.

And then that single finger becomes the flat weight of her palm.

No one else at the table notices.

But Rio’s entire body goes still. Tense.

She turns her head just slightly—slow enough not to draw attention—and meets Agatha’s gaze beside her.

Agatha doesn’t say a word. Doesn’t smirk, doesn’t blink.

Just looks at her over the rim of those crooked glasses. Steady. Calm. Like she’s daring her to react.

Her hand stays right there. The entire dinner.

It never moves. Not once.

No teasing stroke. No subtle squeeze. Just her palm resting firm and warm on Rio’s thigh like it belongs there.

Agatha’s hand seems to pull her out of the spiral currently happening in her head about Wanda. It’s grounding. Solid. 

And Rio’s not sure how Agatha knew she needed that. 

She barely tracks the conversation around her.

Billy is still going, full volume, animated hands flailing as he tells some long-winded story about school drop-off lines and a rogue raccoon. Alice interrupts every few minutes just to call him dramatic. Jen interjects now and then to stop them from setting the table on fire.

Agatha hardly speaks. But when she laughs—quiet and low—it vibrates straight through Rio’s leg. And every time she shifts in her seat, her hand stays exactly where it is. Like it’s glued to her. Like it never occurred to her to move it.

Then Jen signs the check and she stands, suddenly all motion and efficiency. “Alright, circus freaks. Let’s go. You’re welcome for dinner.”

It shouldn’t hit Rio like it does.

But it does.

That dumb little line—you’re welcome for dinner, freaks—lands somewhere warm and stupid in her chest.

She doesn’t say anything. Just follows quietly.

Gets in the backseat when Jen swings the door open.

Billy calls shotgun immediately—loud and victorious—before anyone else can claim it.

Which leaves Rio and Agatha squeezed in the back with Alice. Shoulder to shoulder. Thigh to thigh.

Agatha’s had a couple drinks. Not enough to be sloppy. But enough to be loose.

Her body leans easier. Her laugh slips out softer, more freely. When she slides in beside Rio, she doesn’t hesitate—just lets herself sink in, lets their legs press together like it’s natural.

Her hand finds Rio’s knee again. Casual. Confident. Like she’s been waiting all night to get back to it. Rio’s behind Billy so he can’t see the movement. And it’s dark in the car - even Rio can’t really see her hand. And maybe the hand will stay like it did during dinner and Rio will can stop gay panicking. 

Rio is wrong. 

Agatha’s hand moves.

Just barely. Small circles, slow and steady. The barest motion of her thumb against Rio’s jeans.

All while keeping her face forward. Smiling at something Billy says. Tossing in a dry comment here and there. 

They pull up to Agatha’s house first.

Rio has to climb out to let Agatha out. She doesn’t want to. Agatha’s hand is still on her thigh like a dare. But she moves anyway, opens the door, slides out into the night air that suddenly feels too sharp, too real—and then Agatha moves.

Follows.

Grabs the hem of Rio’s shirt to stop her. Just a gentle tug. Barely there. But Rio feels it like lightning down her spine.

Agatha leans in, voice sweet and casual and drunk as hell. “Hey—I’ll get Rio to her hotel. Just worry about Alice.”

Jesus fucking Christ.

She could not be more obvious if she tried.

Rio just stares at her. Because—what?

Agatha can’t drive. She’s tipsy at best, wasted at worst. And Rio’s “broken-down van” is fine—sitting untouched in the hotel parking lot. 

Alice giggles. Actually giggles. Then slaps a hand over her mouth like she just remembered she’s supposed to be discreet. Her eyes go cartoon-wide. She still throws a thumbs-up from the backseat like a menace.

Rio might actually combust. Because Agatha and Alice are so obvious any outsider could figure out what’s happening here. 

Except maybe Billy.  

Because Billy climbs out, completely unaware. Agatha’s hand drops instantly—like it was never there at all.

Rio catches that Jen’s watching.

Doesn’t say a word. Just gives Rio a long, unreadable look.

And shakes her head.

Billy, loud and cheerful, cuts right through whatever her and Jen have going on -

“Wanda said she’s turning the corner and will be here in just a second!”

Agatha jumps. Barely. 

Rio’s heart slams against her ribs.

Wanda again? Twice in one night?

Her mind goes blank for a second. Then panic kicks in. Maybe it won’t be a disaster. 

But Agatha’s already pulling back. Too composed. “Do you need anything before you go?” she asks Billy, like none of this is happening.

Billy grins. “Maybe just your cooking. Ooh—and soap! I’ll go grab it.”

And then he’s jogging toward the house like this is all normal. The door bangs open behind him.

Agatha turns slowly on her heel, arms folding loose over her chest. And when she looks back at Rio—her whole expression shifts.

Soft. A little smug. Pleased with herself.

“Before you say anything,” she says, already grinning, “it was Alice’s idea.”

Rio blinks. “What was?”

“She wants to talk to Jen alone about the wedding.” Agatha shrugs. Feigning innocence. “It just works out that you’re at my house right now.”

Of course.

The plan. The not-so-subtle conspiracy to derail a wedding.

But that look Jen gave her earlier—that wasn’t just about the car ride or saving her a seat. Jen knew. Not everything. But something. She’s picking up threads, pulling at them.

Rio doesn’t have time to sort it out. And honestly, right now, she doesn’t want to.

She has Agatha right in front of her. 

Even if Wanda is coming. 

It probably won’t be a disaster. 

So she plays along, casual. Teasing. “Just at your house? Or do I get the grand tour? Maybe start with your room?”

Agatha pauses. Just a second. Then there it is—that look. Her eyes shift, darken. Her smirk sharpens like a blade.

Good. Rio can do this.

She still has things to say. About Wanda. About everything.

But then—

Headlights.

Bright and sudden, cutting across the driveway, painting everything in sharp contrast. Cold light on skin. On shadows. 

Just like that, Rio’s yanked back to reality.

Out of the warmth of Agatha’s gaze.

Out of the quiet, reckless possibility of the moment.

Back to her.

Wanda.

The car door opens.

Too slow. Rio should’ve moved. Should’ve dragged Agatha inside the second Billy went for the damn soap. But she stood here instead—flirting like a fool. 

Every time Agatha’s near, she forgets how to think through something - anything. All thoughts just leave her. 

Agatha steps back. A full step.

Rio watches the rise and fall of her chest as she takes a slow breath. Bracing herself. For the same reason Rio’s bracing her own self.

Wanda.

Yeah. This might go bad.

Wanda steps out of the car - left still running in the street. 

Agatha tries anyway. Her voice calm. “He’s just grabbing soap or something. He’ll be right here.”

But Wanda doesn’t even glance at her. Doesn’t blink.

Her eyes are locked on Rio. Cold. Sharp. Like she’s aiming.

And Rio feels it. Deep.

Agatha notices. Of course she does.

But Rio can’t look at her right now. Doesn’t want to see her face. Doesn’t want to see the reaction to what’s about to unfold.

Still, Agatha tries to introduce them, “Wanda, this is Rio—”

Wanda cuts her off. Quick. Final. “I’m very aware.”

That’s it. That’s all it takes.

Rio’s eyes snap to hers. Sharp. What the hell is that supposed to mean?

Agatha glances between them, trying to catch up. Trying to fill in the blanks between Wanda’s clipped words and Rio’s too-stiff posture.

The silence goes long and strange.

But before anyone can speak—

Billy bursts back through the door. Soap in one hand, something shoved in his mouth. He looks ridiculous. 

“Found it!” he yells through a mouthful.

He wipes his hand on his jeans like that helps, then pulls Agatha into a hug. She lets him. A quick squeeze, a pat on the back.

“Tomorrow you’re free from wedding stuff,” she says, stepping away. “But I’m picking you up tomorrow night. We’ve got the rehearsal dinner the next day, so no sneaking out of town.”

Billy laughs. “Okay, no problem.”

And then—surprise—he turns to Rio. Doesn’t hesitate. Wraps her in a hug like they’re old friends.

“Cool to see you again, Rio.”

She freezes. Just a second. Then hugs him back lightly. “Yeah. You too.”

He hops down the driveway like this is the easiest night of his life. Climbs into Wanda’s car, still chewing.

Wanda lingers. Shakes her head. Then gets in the car. 

Rio watches the entire scene. Wanda's hands on the wheel. Eyes forward.

She looks like she wants to say something. Her jaw moves. Her fingers tap the leather once.

Then she shakes her head.

And drives away. 

Rio turns back to Agatha.

She’s still flushed from the alcohol earlier tonight—cheeks warm, lips parted, eyes soft.

Breathtaking.

Rio smiles, just a little. She can do this.

She has to.

“I need to talk to you about something.”

She’s not sure if this plan is going to work - she’s not even sure there is a real plan except keep Jen occupied while Alice says whatever she wants to Ralph. 

She’s not sure about the contract - she just keeps getting stuck on the whole twelve consecutive months part. 

Rio’s pretty sure she’s not sure about anything. 

Except - she’s sure she likes being sat next to Agatha. 

Even if she’s not staying. Even if this is temporary.

Even if it’s all about to fall apart. 

Still—Agatha’s next to her. 

Talking about Billy’s book.

——

They pull into Evanora’s driveway and the dread hits her like clockwork.

The kind that settles in her gut, heavy and old. Doesn’t matter how nice the house looks in the early evening light—clean porch, fresh paint, those too-perfect bushes lining the walk—it still feels like a mausoleum. Cold and sharp around the edges.

Billy’s already unclipping his seatbelt before the car’s even in park. Agatha doesn’t move.

“Billy,” she says, just loud enough. “We’ll catch up. Go ahead.”

He gives a thumbs up and keeps going, jogging up the porch steps just as Jen opens the front door. She spots him, grins wide, and pulls him into a hug—arm wrapping around him, whispering something in his ear. Her laugh echoes before the door clicks shut behind them.

And then—Rio barely has a second to turn back—Agatha’s lips are on hers.

A surprise. Fast and urgent.

Rio kisses back immediately, hand instinctively cupping Agatha’s cheek, grounding them both for a second.

And just as quick, Agatha pulls back.

They’re still close. Still breathing the same air. Agatha’s breath is brushing against her lips—warm puffs, soft and uneven.

She doesn’t move. Neither of them do.

Rio’s voice is low when she speaks, still catching up to what just happened. “What was that for?”

Agatha just smiles, small and soft. “You look good. That’s all.”

Rio watches her for a beat longer. Agatha’s eyes are steady. Her mouth is still pink from the kiss.

Rio glances down at the clock on the dash. Twenty minutes before they’re supposed to be seated inside, pretending everything’s fine.

She exhales slow. “Evanora’s got a greenhouse,” she says, voice casual but threading a line between hope and mischief. “It’s where I’m keeping all the flowers for the wedding.”

Agatha arches a brow. “You’re storing them here?”

“Didn’t have a choice,” Rio says, already reaching for the door handle. “But I do have to check on them. Make sure everything’s still upright and hydrated and untouched by disaster.”

Agatha’s watching her closely.

Rio shrugs, meeting her gaze. “Want to come with me?”

She doesn’t say before we walk into that house or before I have to pretend this place doesn’t make my skin itch. She’s pretty sure Agatha already knows anyhow. 

But, Agatha’s already nodding. “Lead the way.”

And Rio’s already climbing out, heart hammering a little faster.

Because maybe this isn’t just about checking on the flowers.

Maybe she just needs a few more minutes. Just her and Agatha. Before the show starts.

They step into the greenhouse and the air shifts. Warm and thick with green. Not humid—controlled. The kind of air Rio knows how to breathe.

Agatha’s standing just inside the doorway. Blinking around.

“Wow,” she says, voice low. “Rio—there’s so many.”

Rio smiles. She gets to work. Checks the water lines, the temp gauge, the petals on the farthest batch of roses. Everything’s still holding. Healthy. Blooming. She doesn’t say it, but the flowers look perfect.

They’ll hold through the wedding.

She turns back and—

Agatha’s watching her. Eyebrows pulled together. Finger pressed to her lips.

Rio stills. “What’s that look for?”

Agatha doesn’t answer at first. Just stares across the greenhouse like she’s trying to see through it.

Then, finally—quiet: “Nothing, it’s just…”

Rio waits. Doesn’t push. But she wants the answer.

“Tell me.”

Agatha shifts. “Jen would’ve never picked roses. Not even for a funeral, let alone her wedding.”

That stops something in Rio. She stands straighter. Feels it—panic starting to tap on the door.

“Agatha,” she says slowly , “they were in the contract. A thousand roses. I double-checked. Evanora signed. Jen called me personally. Asked to confirm. Red roses.”

Agatha doesn’t look away. Doesn’t even blink. “I believe you,” she says. “I’m just telling you—she hates them.”

Rio exhales. Tries to catch the crack before it gets bigger. “Then maybe it wasn’t her call.”

Agatha tilts her head.

“Could’ve been Evanora,” Rio says. “Or worse. Ralph.”

That gets a laugh. Sharp and bitter and too loud for the space.

“Well,” Agatha says, still smiling, “now I don’t feel as guilty for trying to ruin the wedding. Tragic. These beautiful flowers. Wasted.”

Rio steps closer. Not touching. But close.

Agatha looks up at her. Her smile doesn’t falter. But there’s something in her eyes now. Something deeper.

Rio leans in. Slow. Teasing. She’s so close to Agatha she can practically taste her breath—minty from the toothpaste earlier. She’s about to kiss her, just about to press their mouths together when she pulls back at the last second, grinning.

“C’mon,” she murmurs, voice low and rough. “Before Billy catches us in here.”

Agatha doesn’t care. Not even a little. She closes the space between them and kisses Rio anyway—quick, firm, like she needed one more before they went back to pretending everything’s normal. “Fine,” she says against Rio’s mouth. “Let’s go.”

She turns like she means it, already halfway out of the greenhouse, and Rio’s hands move before her brain can stop them. She catches Agatha’s wrist gently, tugs her back. Not hard. Not demanding. Just enough to pull her back.

One more kiss. A little slower this time. Not desperate, not yet, but close.

“Sorry,” Rio says when they finally pull apart again. Her voice is quieter now. “Don’t kiss a lot of ladies in front of a thousand roses.”

Agatha actually laughs. One of those deep, bright ones that catches Rio off guard every single time. “It would be so romantic,” she says, shaking her head, “if these weren’t the roses from my best friend’s wedding that we’re actively trying to ruin.”

And then she’s turning again, walking out like none of that just happened. Like she didn’t just say something that cracked Rio’s chest open.

Romantic.

Rio stays still for a beat too long. Watches the way the sun catches in Agatha’s hair as she walks out the greenhouse door. Watches how easily she moves, how lightly she leaves.

And the word lingers.

Romantic.

Fuck. It would be. That’s the worst part.

It is.

She’s not supposed to feel it like this—not when there’s still so much up in the air. Not when she hasn’t even signed the contract Kate sent over. Not when there’s a thousand fucking roses right in front of her that might end up in the trash if this whole thing burns down. Not when Agatha isn’t hers. Not really.

But the word is still there, stuck in her throat. Rio feels like it’s choking her.

She exhales hard through her nose and finally moves, following Agatha out and into the evening sun. The front lawn’s starting to fill in. People she doesn’t recognize, all dressed up, arriving in pairs. Light chatter from the front steps. Someone laughs too loud. The kind of sound that makes Rio feel like she’s on the outside of something.

Agatha’s a few steps ahead now, already halfway up the walk, blending in effortlessly. Rio’s not surprised. Agatha belongs in places like this. Polished and composed, even when she’s trying to quietly dismantle a wedding from the inside out.

Rio glances down at her feet as she walks, adjusting her jacket. One breath at a time. That’s the plan.

She’ll be fine.

She’s sitting next to Billy and Jen. They’ll keep her distracted.

And she’ll keep Jen distracted. 

Focus on the plan. 

They get seated, and Rio feels her stomach drop as soon as she sees where everyone ends up. Jen’s next to Evanora. Which means Rio’s also pretty close to Evanora. Great.

She clocks Agatha’s glance from across the table—subtle, barely a lift of her brows—but Rio catches it anyway. She doesn’t smile back. Just shifts in her seat and picks up her water.

It’s fine. She can get through this. One dinner.

The first few minutes aren’t bad. Food’s served—some fancy plated chicken and vegetables, with flowers on top that actually make Billy perk up.

“Are these real?” he asks, jabbing his fork at the petals.

Rio leans toward him. “Yeah. Those purple ones are violas, and the orange is marigold. Both edible.”

“No way.” He grins. “That’s so cool. Are they good?”

“Marigold’s a little bitter. Violas are mild though. Add some color. Some people candy them.”

Billy looks impressed. He asks another question, and another, until Rio’s talking without thinking. Just like in her shop—facts and small stories, comfort in rhythm. Aloe plants, succulents, what grows best in shade. She forgets where she is for a second. It helps.

She catches Agatha excusing herself to the restroom - has to force herself to not watch her walk away. 

Jen joins in when Billy brings up aloe again. “It’s good for skin,” she says, eyes still on her plate. “Cools down sunburns, moisturizes. I used to use it all the time as a kid.”

It’s simple. Casual. Rio starts to relax.

But of course, the calm doesn’t last.

“Rio,” Evanora says, voice soft but pointed, “how’s business these days?”

It’s not an innocent question. Nothing from Evanora ever is.

Rio chews slowly. Swallows. “It’s good,” she says, short and neutral. Keep it tight. Keep it clean.

Evanora’s smile sharpens. “Well, florists can’t make too much, can they?” she muses. “I mean, my contract with you must be the best you’ve seen in months—if not years. Am I correct?”

Rio sets her fork down. She exhales.

God, she hates her.

It takes everything in her not to snap. She can feel the table shifting. Subtle glances. People pausing in their conversations. Waiting.

She shouldn’t say anything. She knows she shouldn’t.

But she’s not going to let Evanora play her like that. She can’t help herself. 

“Actually,” Rio says, tone smooth but firm, “I’m negotiating a contract with a company that would set me up for the next year. Maybe longer.”

Silence, for just a second.

Evanora smiles. Tighter this time. “Good for you.”

Rio doesn’t look at her. Doesn’t give her the satisfaction.

She glances to the side instead—just in time to catch Jen’s eyes.

Her expression is… unreadable.

Not mad. Not surprised either. Just watching.

And something about it twists in Rio’s chest.

Rio looks away.

She reaches for her water again just to have something to do with her hands, her mind racing. Not because she regrets what she said—screw Evanora—but because she hadn’t told Agatha. Not about the offer. Not about how serious it was. Not about how real it suddenly feels.

And now it’s out there. In front of Jen. In front of everyone. Well - not everyone. 

Agatha just came and sat back down.

Luckily for Rio, Ralph stands up with a clink of his fork against his glass, grinning like he just invented love itself.

“To love,” he says, loud and booming like he’s at his wedding already.

Rio nearly chokes on her water.

“To love,” Ralph repeats, raising his glass higher. “To the magic that brought us together. To the soul-deep connection that withstands the tests of time. And to new beginnings—our marriage, and our move to Colorado… next month!”

He smiles like he just pulled off the greatest mic drop in engagement history.

Rio doesn’t roll her eyes—but barely. Jen and Evanora are right there. She keeps her face neutral. 

She chances a glance across the table.

Agatha’s eyebrows are halfway up her forehead. Alice actually mutters, “What the fuck?” under her breath.

Agatha says it out loud: “Next month?”

Jen’s head whips toward Ralph. “Next month? It was supposed to be next year.”

Ralph, undeterred, walks over to Jen and Rio, leans in toward her like this is a moment she’s going to swoon over. “I wanted to surprise you, babe! I already bought the house and everything. It’s all set. We’re gonna get a head start!”

He says it like it’s romantic. Like she’s going to leap into his arms.

Rio watches Jen blink. Twice. Her face still. Too still.

Evanora, of course, chooses now to chime in, hands clapping together softly. “Oh, this will be great! Get ahead of it before the new year! There’s so much opportunity in Colorado, Jennifer.”

And that’s it.

Jen’s jaw clenches. Her voice doesn’t rise at first—but it’s sharp. “No.”

The room stills.

“No,” she repeats. “This is not what we agreed on.”

Ralph blinks at her, like she’s the one being unreasonable.

“What do you mean? I thought this would be—”

“You thought,” Jen cuts in, her voice louder now, “without talking to me.”

She’s not yelling. Not quite. But the entire room’s quiet now. There’s at least twenty people in the dining room, forks mid-air, wine glasses paused halfway to lips. All of them frozen, watching it happen.

“This isn’t what we discussed,” Jen says. Her voice is shaking a little now. “It was supposed to be next year. What about everything here in Westview?”

“We’ll figure it out,” Ralph says, still smiling like he can talk his way through it. “I figured you’d be excited! I got us this perfect place—”

“That’s not the point, Ralph.”

There’s no mistaking her tone now. She’s not smiling. She’s not performing.

And Rio?

She just sits there and watches it unravel.

Jen’s face is flushed. Ralph looks stunned. Agatha’s hand has gone tight around her wine glass. Alice is staring daggers across the table, and Evanora’s plastered smile is still frozen on her face like she can’t quite process what’s going wrong.

Rio doesn’t know all the details.

But she’s getting the picture pretty damn fast.

And it doesn’t look good.

Jen stands. “If you’ll excuse me,” she says, and she’s gone—just like that.

Alice is out of her chair in an instant. Agatha too. No hesitation.

They both follow, leaving Billy seated next to Rio.

Rio stays frozen, stunned. That wasn’t the plan. That wasn’t supposed to happen yet. They hadn’t even started the plan - not really anyway. 

“Woah,” Billy mutters under his breath.

Rio exhales. Yeah. That about covers it.

Evanora stands, still somehow composed, even as the dinner guests whisper around them. “Thank you for coming to dinner,” she announces. Her voice floats across the table like the host of some dead silent game show. “I need to speak with my daughter.”

Rio’s jaw clenches at that. Her daughter. Hits the same every damn time.

The dining room starts clearing out. Guests murmuring, collecting purses, coats, awkward glances passed like secret notes.

Rio turns to Billy. “C’mon. Let’s go find something to do.”

He looks up at her, eyebrow raised. “What, don’t wanna be in that room?”

Rio snorts. “Not especially. And I’m not leaving you to fend for yourself.”

Billy laughs, and Rio steers them both out through the back door. It’s cooler now. Evening. She leads them back toward the greenhouse, one of the only spaces on this property that feels like hers.

Once they’re inside, Rio checks on the roses again, even though she already did it earlier. All of them look the same—fed, upright, undisturbed. But Billy’s the one who gets wide-eyed.

“Whoa,” he says, walking the row like he’s at a museum. “There’s so many.”

“Thousand roses,” Rio says. “Every one of them accounted for.”

He hums, crouching to peer at a bloom. Rio leans back against one of the counters, arms crossed. She lets herself breathe. The greenhouse smells like soil and cut stems and sunlight trapped from earlier. Not peace, exactly. But close enough.

It’s quiet for a bit. Billy doesn’t seem to mind. He just drifts from one flower to the next, totally fascinated.

Then, casually, too casually, he says, “So… don’t shoot the messenger—”

“Oh Jesus,” Rio mutters, already bracing. “What?”

Billy shrugs. “But… why does Wanda hate you so much?”

Rio closes her eyes for a beat. Of course.

“She doesn’t hate me,” Rio says, trying to keep it light, but her voice comes out flatter than she wants. “She just… has opinions.”

“Yeah, she told me you were selfish and that you always leave,” Billy says, still crouched by a flower like he’s talking about the weather.

Rio blinks. Jesus Christ. Wanda really is harsh. “Wow. Direct quote?”

He nods. “Pretty much. I mean, she said it nicer, but like… not really?”

Rio lets out a breath, scrubs a hand down her face. “Great. Cool.”

Billy stands. “But I don’t think you’re that bad.”

“That bad, huh?” she echoes.

He grins. “I mean you just saved us both from whatever’s going on in there. And you seem to make Aunt Jen happy. And Agatha- even Alice a little bit.”

Rio huffs a laugh, but there’s a knot in her stomach she can’t quite untie. Wanda. Bad-mouthing her. To Billy. She doesn’t even know what part of her Wanda told him about. Doesn’t really want to know.

Rio snorts and lets her head fall back against the wall. “Yeah - they uh - they’re making me pretty happy too.”

And for a moment—it’s quiet again. The only place on the property where no one’s fighting. 

She hears footsteps. Sharp ones, purposeful. Rio glances toward the greenhouse door, straightening up a little. Thank God. Agatha, probably. Come to find them. Ready to drive them both back and get the hell out of this nightmare dinner.

But the person who turns the corner isn’t Agatha.

It’s Jen.

Rio blinks. Surprised, but maybe not as much as she should be. Tonight’s been one thing after another. What’s one more?

“Hey,” Jen says, lingering in the doorway. “Agatha’s inside. She’s looking for you.”

Billy steps toward her, already moving, polite as always. “Thanks,” he says.

But Jen stops him with a hand on his arm before he gets through the door. “Hey—thanks for putting up with all the wedding stuff. I know it sucks. But you’ve been awesome.”

Billy softens at that. Smile kind of shy. “Anything for you, Aunt Jen.”

And then he’s gone, walking back toward the house. They both watch him go.

Jen’s quiet for a second longer than is comfortable.

Rio shifts her weight. Waiting. Bracing.

Jen turns back around, takes a slow step into the greenhouse. Her eyes move over the space. The rows of roses. The careful work.

“Wow,” she says. “Rio. These are… gorgeous.”

Rio huffs out a dry laugh. “You don’t have to lie, Jen. Agatha told me. You hate roses.”

Jen’s eyes snap back to hers. Sharp. A little defensive.

“You’re right. I do hate them.” She takes another step closer. “But I still think the work you would’ve done with them is beautiful.”

It hits right in the chest. Too fast. Too much.

Would’ve.

Rio swallows. Her throat suddenly feels thick. Tight.

She tries to shake it off, to joke, but it doesn’t come out right. “Would’ve done with them, huh?” she says, voice thinner than she wants. “Did you call it off?”

Jen’s mouth pulls into a frown. Like maybe she hadn’t meant to say it like that. Like maybe she’s realizing the weight of her own words just now.

“I don’t know,” Jen says quietly. “Maybe.”

Rio just nods, her hands still dug into the counter behind her. Silent. Because if she opens her mouth right now, she’s not sure what would come out.

Jen crosses her arms, still looking around at the roses like she’s searching for something to say. Rio figures maybe this is where the conversation ends. But then Jen speaks up again, “So what’s the company you’re signing with?”

Rio’s caught off guard for a second. “What?”

“That contract. You mentioned it at dinner.”

Oh. Right. That.

Rio lets out a slow breath, shifts back against the counter again. “It’s with Kate—Kate Bishop. She runs a high-end events firm out of the city. Has a ton of corporate clients, a lot of money thrown around for centerpiece bullshit. But she’s good. She’s solid. And she’s giving me a full year’s contract, booked out.” A pause. “Guaranteed.”

Jen nods, taking it in, expression unreadable.

Then Rio adds, quieter, like she’s admitting something she shouldn’t be: “I haven’t signed it yet.”

Jen’s eyebrows shoot up. “Then why the hell did you tell mom that you did?”

Rio shrugs, but there’s tension in her shoulders. “Because I didn’t want to deal with her. Evanora acts like being a florist is a fucking hobby. Like I should be grateful she gave me your wedding. It was easier to shut her up than explain why I haven’t signed yet.”

Jen narrows her eyes. “Mom didn’t give you the wedding, I asked for you.” Jen shakes her head, “Doesn’t matter. why haven’t you signed yet?”

Rio doesn’t answer.

Not right away.

She knows why. And it has nothing to do with the ink or the logistics or the client list. It has everything to do with a plan she and Agatha made that suddenly doesn’t feel as clear-cut. Everything to do with a goodbye she’s supposed to say in a few days, and how it might not be as easy as she told herself it would be.

She clears her throat. “I will. It’s not like I’m backing out. I just… haven’t made it official yet.”

Jen quirks an eyebrow. Still watching her. Still too sharp.

“When are you going to tell Agatha?”
