Twenty-Four

Chapter Summary

Agatha’s POV

Chapter Notes

another update?
another update!
no porn all plot again 😔
🩸🧪?

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Jen walks out of the dining room, and Agatha’s already on her feet. Alice is right behind her. The three of them trail down the hallway before they end up in Jen’s old bedroom. 

Same paint. Same queen-sized bed with the curved headboard and fairy lights still hanging above it like some kind of time capsule. Agatha’s eyes flick to the shelves—still lined with books Jen probably hasn’t touched in years. She doesn’t know why she notices that.

Jen’s pacing now. Barefoot, furious, muttering to herself like she’s halfway to losing it.

“I can’t believe this. I can’t believe I have absolutely no control over my life.”

Alice tries to step in. “Okay, hey, sit down, let’s just—”

She reaches out gently, hand to Jen’s elbow. Jen brushes it off without a second thought, still pacing, still spiraling.

Agatha’s had enough.

“Jen.” She doesn’t respond or stop. 

Louder, “Jen.” 

Nothing. Okay. Full naming the woman then - loud. 

“Jennifer.”

It snaps her like a whip. She freezes mid-step, eyes wide like she forgot they were even in the room.

“Let’s all sit,” Agatha says, motioning to the bed. “Come on.”

Jen doesn’t argue. Not really. She just exhales, sharp and shallow, and drops onto the edge of the bed like her knees gave out. Alice hovers a second longer before sitting beside her. Agatha stays standing for now, close but not crowding them.

“Okay,” she says. Calm. Solid. “Deep breath.”

Jen does it. Not gracefully. Not easily. But she does it.

Agatha nods once. “Let’s talk about this, Jen. What are you thinking?”

Alice jumps in too fast, too loud.

“Yeah—Colorado?! You can’t go to Colorado!”

Agatha shoots her a look. Sharp. Just enough to cut.

“Alice. Not important right now.”

Alice clamps her mouth shut, eyes darting between them.

Agatha turns back to Jen. Quieter this time. “What are you thinking?”

Jen’s eyes flick up to meet hers. Tired. A little wet around the edges, but not crying. She’s trying to keep it together. Trying to breathe.

Agatha waits. Doesn’t fill the silence.

Jen exhales like it physically hurts. Like the breath itself weighs something.

“I’m not doing it,” she says finally, voice low. “I’m not making any more decisions just for everyone else. I can’t.”

Alice reaches out, rubs both hands along Jen’s arms like she’s trying to calm a storm. Jen doesn’t shake her off this time.

“He can’t do that. Ralph can’t just make that decision. Go behind my back, tell everyone we’re moving to Colorado like I don’t even get a vote. Like I’m just gonna follow him because he’s already packed the car.”

Agatha stays quiet. Watches her.

“And Mom—” Jen laughs, bitter, short. “She’s been planning my entire life since I was in high school. Maybe earlier. You remember that, don’t you?”

Agatha does. Clear as day. Jen in that exact room, furious because Evanora had given her a timeline. University, internships, engagement by twenty-eight. The dress. The venue. A four-bedroom house and a golden retriever. Like it was a job application she’d already failed if she wanted something different.

“She picked the date,” Jen’s still going. “She picked the colors. The venue. The stupid favors. You know I didn’t even choose the damn band? Ralph did. And she approved it. They didn’t even ask me.”

Alice mutters, “That’s insane,” but Jen’s already rolling, voice sharper now.

“The dress? I didn’t pick the dress either. I tried on one that I liked and mom made a face and that was it. She said it didn’t suit me. That I should wear something timeless.”

She goes quiet for a second. Then quieter.

“I asked if Rio could come just to do the flowers,” she says. “And she got mad. Said it would be a distraction. Said it was stupid to even bother.”

Agatha feels something twist in her chest.

“Maybe we weren’t close,” Jen keeps going, eyes on the floor now. “Maybe we didn’t grow up braided-at-the-wrist close. But she’s my sister. My sister. And she got upset. Like that wasn’t allowed.”

Agatha shifts closer, kneels in front of her. She wants to reach out, but doesn’t yet.

“Jen,” she says, soft but firm. “You’re allowed to want your sister at your wedding.”

Jen nods. Slowly. Like she’s just now giving herself permission to believe it.

Jen keeps going. “I don’t know what’s going to happen,” she says, dragging both hands through her hair, pacing again. “But I cannot do this anymore.” She turns, meets Agatha’s eyes. “Like—maybe Rio’s out of the will or whatever, but at least she’s free of it. She doesn’t have to sit through dinners pretending to agree with mom. She doesn’t have to fake it through a wedding she didn’t choose.”

Agatha stays quiet, but the words hit sharp. Not because they’re wrong. No - because they’re true.

“I was always so envious of her,” Jen continues. “How Mom never tried to control her. Not really.”

And Agatha thinks—because she can’t help it—Evanora didn’t control her because she hated Rio. Because she made sure Rio knew exactly where she stood. Rio just told her that. But Agatha doesn’t say it. Not now.

“I watched her this week,” Jen’s voice softens, like she’s talking to herself more than them. “And I don’t even know her that well, not really. But damn—she just does whatever she wants. Doesn’t second guess. Doesn’t apologize. Doesn’t worry about the fallout until it’s in front of her.”

Agatha swallows. 

“I want that,” Jen says. “I need that. I want to want something and not immediately hear Mom’s voice in my head telling me why I shouldn’t.”

Silence settles over the room like a weighted blanket. Thick. Heavy.

“I can’t marry Ralph,” Jen says. Not a whisper. Not a scream. Just… final.

Agatha stands, wraps her arms around her without hesitating. “We’re here for every step, babe.”

Alice folds in on the other side, sniffling. “Plus, who needs Evanora’s money anyway? I’ve seen your savings. You could do that skincare line you’ve always wanted.”

Jen actually laughs. Wet and tired and real. She wipes her eyes with the back of her hand. “Maybe I’ll just follow Rio to New York. Mooch off her and her big new contract.”

Agatha stiffens. Pulls back just slightly. “Wait. What contract?”

Agatha catches it immediately—the look Alice gives her. Quick, subtle, but not subtle enough. Like she knows something she shouldn’t. Like she’s waiting to see how Agatha reacts.

Then she looks at Jen. Same look.

Jen doesn’t say a word. But her eyes are saying plenty.

Alice jumps in before Agatha can ask. “She just mentioned it at dinner. The contract. Said she’ll be set for like… the next year, working events in New York.”

New York.

And fuck does that do a number on Agatha’s chest. Like someone reached in and pulled a thread loose.

Because she should be happy. 

She is happy for her. 

It’s exactly what Rio deserves—traction, money, freedom.

But that contract isn’t here. That contract is in New York.

Jen nods like it’s no big deal. Like this is all normal. Like Agatha’s lungs aren’t suddenly tightening like fists.

“Yeah,” Jen adds, casually, but she’s watching her. Really watching. “She seemed - I don’t know, proud maybe? Seems like a big deal kind of thing.”

Agatha feels everything all at once. Heart pounding. Skin prickling. A little dizzy.

She could puke. Or scream. Or get in her car and drive somewhere far enough that it doesn’t hurt to think about Rio leaving.

But instead she just nods. Once. Sharp.

“Good for her,” she says, voice even. Flat. A lie wrapped in pride.

Because it is good. And she is proud. 

But she’s not happy about it. 

And it still hurts like hell.

And then -

Jen hums, quiet but sharp. “Is it?”

Agatha blinks. “Is what?”

Jen leans forward. “Is it good for her?”

Agatha scoffs, quick. “Of course it is. It’s a huge opportunity. I’m—” her voice goes tight, “—I’m happy for her.”

Jen doesn’t blink. “Agatha, you’re allowed to be upset about Rio’s contract.”

Agatha’s eyes narrow. “Why would I be upset about your sister’s contract?” 

What the fuck does Jen know?

Silence stretches. Alice is staring at Jen now, mouth slightly open. Agatha watches them both, something turning in her gut.

Jen just shrugs, like the answer’s obvious. “Come on, Agatha. I’m not stupid. You had a hickey during the facial.”

Agatha’s stomach drops. Her spine goes rigid. She opens her mouth—no, fuck, what is she even supposed to say to that? Her voice scrambles to defend her before her brain can catch up. “That wasn’t a—”

Jen holds up a finger. “Don’t lie.”

Agatha’s mouth shuts. Hard.

“I knew this whole time,” Jen says, voice low. “Come on, you were flirting with her at the bar. I saw it.”

Agatha blurts, fast, panicked, “I didn’t know it was Rio at the time—”

Jen cuts in without missing a beat. “Sure. But what about you being insanely jealous over the  waitress at the spa resort? Or the fact that you were very much in the middle of something when I brought you your extra room key? Or that you both conveniently missed breakfast?”

Agatha wants to melt into the fucking floor.

Jen keeps going, not cruel, just honest. “What about when I drove you home, and Rio stayed? Do you really think I didn’t notice all of that?”

Agatha presses her lips together. She’s not sure if she’s mad or embarrassed or just unraveling.

“Don’t lie to me,” Jen says, softer now. “I’m not mad. Not about that. You seem… happy. Or lighter. Different than when you were with Wanda.”

Agatha blinks fast. Those words, specifically—happy—lands like a bruise.

“I am mad you hid it from me,” Jen says, “but I get it. I get why you did.”

Agatha exhales and softens, reaching across to touch Jen’s arm. “Oh, honey. I’m sorry. I didn’t want to add more stress to you—not during your wedding.”

Jen lets out a surprised laugh, shaky and real.

Before Agatha can respond, Alice throws her hands up. “Oh thank fuck. I’ve been dying to talk about this forever with you guys.”

Jen snorts, shakes her head, but her smile’s still there. Agatha arches a brow at her. 

Jen shifts, voice quieter now. “Agatha… you deserve to be happy too. Especially after the last few years.”

That lands. That one stings in a different way. Not in a bad way, just… deep.

“And Billy loves her,” Jen adds. “So yes - you are allowed to be upset about the contract.”

Agatha swallows. Her hands twist together in her lap. “We, um — we agreed that this would be over. After your wedding. Whatever this - us - is.”

Silence settles over the room again. Jen looks down. Alice looks at Jen. Neither of them speak for a beat.

Then Alice leans forward, voice softer than usual. “Yeah, but that girl looks at you like you put the moon in the fucking sky, Agatha.”

Agatha’s heart clenches. She feels it everywhere—her throat, her chest, her ribs. It hurts. It aches. Like the wind’s been knocked out of her.

Jen claps her hands once. “Okay. I’ve made a life-altering decision tonight. Both of you need to make one as well.”

Agatha raises an eyebrow. “Oh yeah?”

“Yes. Agatha, you’re talking to Rio. And Alice—don’t think you’re getting out of this. We’ll figure one out for you. But both of you are going to make a decision that makes you happy. Mine was possibly cutting myself out of my mother’s very, very large will. No pressure.”

Agatha laughs under her breath, “Low stakes. Got it.”

Jen smacks her knees and stands up. “With that being said—I’m going to get some air before Mom finds me.”

They watch her slip out the door, and it’s quiet for a second.

Then Agatha turns to Alice. She’s still seated, still grinning like a damn Cheshire cat.

“You should talk to her, Agatha,” Alice says, voice light, teasing. “At the very least, you’ll get really hot sex out of it.”

Agatha laughs—quiet and genuine. “You’re disgusting.”

Alice shrugs. “I’m not wrong.”

Agatha shifts. “Fine. But what are you going to do, huh?”

Alice’s smile softens just a touch. A little more real. “I’m going to tell her.”

Agatha blinks. “Tell who what?”

Alice pushes herself off the bed, heading toward the door.

“I’m going to tell Jen I’m in love with her.”

Agatha’s brain short-circuits. 

“What.”

Alice’s already in the hallway.

“WHAT?” Agatha bolts after her. “Alice get your ass back here!”

Alice just laughs as she disappears down the hallway. Agatha’s left standing in the doorway, hands on her head, completely losing her mind.

“Hey, Agatha.”

She jumps.

“Jesus—Billy,” she breathes out, hand to her chest. “You scared the hell out of me.”

He grins like it was on purpose. “Sorry. Are you okay?”

Agatha’s heart softens immediately. “I’m good, sweetheart. Just wanted to make sure Aunt Jen was okay.”

Billy nods, satisfied. “Rio showed me the roses.”

“Oh yeah?”

“Yeah,” he says, eyes wide. “Do you think we’ll get to see them put to use?”

Agatha laughs under her breath. “No, I don’t think so, honey.”

Billy sighs with pure relief. “Oh thank God. I love Aunt Jen, but I don’t think I could sit still in that itchy tux through the whole wedding.”

That earns a real laugh from her. 

“Come here,” she says, ruffling his curls. “Let’s take a second before we find Rio.”

They duck back into Jen’s room for a breather. Billy flops onto the bed like he owns the place, arms folded behind his head, legs too long now to not hang off the edge. 

“You okay?” she asks, voice soft.

“Yeah.” He shrugs.

Agatha lowers herself onto the edge of the bed beside him. For a second, they sit in the kind of stillness that only comes after chaos. The kind that makes you realize how tired you are.

“I like Rio,” Billy says suddenly.

“Oh, yeah?” Agatha answers, casual. Reflexive.

Where the fuck did that come from?

“Yeah, when you and Alice ran after Jen she showed me the greenhouse so we weren’t trapped in that dining room.”

“I’m glad she got you out of there, honey. I’m sorry I ran after Jen.”

“It’s okay. I need to say sorry to her though.”

Agatha turns a little to look at him. “Sorry, for what?”

“I told her what Wanda said about her and I shouldn’t have—I was just trying to tell her that I liked her being around.”

Her chest tightens. That familiar, low-grade panic that always bubbles up at the mention of Wanda. She straightens a little.

“What—um—what did Wanda say, honey?”

Billy glances at her, then away, like he’s debating if it’s worth repeating.

“Oh. Um… she just says she leaves all the time. That she’s selfish. Or something.”

The words hit like a cold slap. She feels her jaw tighten. Of course Wanda said that.

“She said that to you?”

“She didn’t mean to,” Billy says quickly. “She was just… talking. She does that thing where she thinks I’m not listening.”

Agatha breathes in slowly. Nods like it’s no big deal even though her blood is running hot. She’s not mad at Billy. Not even a little. But Wanda? Jesus.

She leans back on her hands and looks up at the ceiling. “Well,” she says finally, “I think Wanda just has some very strong opinions on her.” She turns her head toward him. “Do you think Rio’s selfish?”

“Oh—no. Definitely not.” He shakes his head, firm.

She lets out a slow exhale. “Well, it’s settled then—Wanda’s crazy.”

Billy laughs at that, a real deep laugh. It’s the best sound in the world. 

She reaches over and squeezes his shoulder, standing up. “Come on, honey. Let’s grab Rio and get out of here, shall we?”

He nods enthusiastically, and they get up at the same time. Walking out of the room, she wraps an arm around him. They round the hallway corner—Agatha still warm with the weight of him leaning into her side.

They catch Rio by the front door, already looking ready to bolt. Agatha can tell just from the way she’s standing—shoulders tight, jaw set, eyes scanning for the nearest escape.

Agatha raises a brow. “Ready to blow this popsicle stand?”

Rio’s nodding before she’s even finished the sentence. “Let’s get the fuck out of here, please.”

Agatha doesn’t say anything, just smiles and reaches for the front door. 

They climb into the car, doors shutting quickly like they’re completing a heist . Agatha turns the key in the ignition and shifts into drive, but it’s like her body’s moving on autopilot. 

Because fuck.

That conversation with Jen has settled into her chest like cement.

Rio’s contract.

She grips the steering wheel a little tighter. She has to talk to her. Tonight. Jen basically assigned it to her. And Agatha’s not pushing her luck with Jen any further. The woman knew everything. 

She pulls onto the main road while Billy starts firing questions at Rio about plants—again. Something about sunlight or maybe watering schedules? She’s not really hearing it. Just Rio’s voice answering in that casual way, slipping in a joke now and then to make him laugh.

Agatha doesn’t register half of it. Her mind’s racing. Spinning through timelines and endings and New York contracts and hickeys and Rio’s mouth and—fuck.

Before she knows it, she’s turning onto Wanda’s street. Billy’s already unbuckling. He hops out and then stops at her window, waiting. She rolls it down with a faint smile.

“Should I not tell Wanda about the wedding?”

Agatha lets out a tired laugh. “You don’t need to lie to her, honey.” She sighs, rubbing a hand over her face. “But… maybe don’t bring it up unless she asks, alright?”

Billy grins. “Okay.” He leans in further, waving across her toward Rio. “Bye, Rio. Bye, Agatha.”

“Bye, sweetie,” she calls, watching him walk up the walkway, all long limbs and carefree ease. A beat passes. Then another. 

Rio turns toward her, finally. “Where to next?” she asks, voice gentle. 

“Let’s go back to my place,” Agatha says, trying to sound casual. “There’s wine there at least.”

Rio laughs softly, a bit more ease to her posture. “Okay, Agatha - as you wish.”

The car falls into a gentle silence as Agatha merges onto the highway, headlights cutting through the dim wash of the evening. She’s fine. This is fine. She just has to—talk. Say it. Ask. Something.

And then, both of them open their mouths at the same time.

“Can we—”

“I think—”

They both stop, startled by the timing.

Rio glances over. “Ladies first.”

Agatha exhales a smile. “Can we talk ?” she asks, flicking her gaze toward Rio quickly before returning her focus to the road.

Rio’s smile fades just slightly, replaced with something more grounded, serious. She nods. “Of course, Agatha. That’s what I was going to ask you too.”

Agatha stares ahead, jaw tightening, willing herself not to react. But she feels it anyway. That wave of nerves, crashing harder with every mile they close between them and her front door. Maybe she’s going to say she’s leaving. Maybe she’s going to say it’s over because there’s no wedding and she’s going back tonight. Because the whole plan is off. Because New York —

A warm hand lands on her thigh.

She jumps slightly, not from fear but from the way it pulls her right out of her head.

Rio’s voice is softer now. “Agatha.”

Agatha glances at her again. The concern in Rio’s eyes is clear, and her thumb is rubbing slow, grounding circles against Agatha’s leg.

“Yeah?” she manages, voice rougher than she wants it to be.

Rio hesitates for half a beat. Then she says, “I need to tell you about work. My work.”

Agatha nods once, swallowing hard.

Rio doesn’t let go of her leg. And then she starts. 

“It’s about the call I got earlier today,” she says, voice low, thumb brushing slow and steady against Agatha’s thigh. “It’s from a woman named Kate Bishop. She owns or is part of this high-end event planning company in New York. Real deal. She’s been looking for a florist.”

Agatha keeps her eyes straight ahead, trying to breathe like it’s normal. Like her lungs aren’t tight.

“The contract’s…” Rio exhales a quiet laugh. “It’s ridiculous, Agatha. Financial freedom. Straight up. A monthly retainer that would cover everything. Rent. Groceries. I could stop taking bad clients. Stop doing back-to-back parties every weekend just to keep my business above water.”

She pauses, her fingers stilling for just a second, then moving again.

“I could be picky. Finally. Choose the projects I actually care about.”

Agatha nods once. She remembers the call now—Rio stepping outside the kitchen this morning with her phone when Alice came over. She didn’t think anything of it at the time. 

Rio goes on. “I mentioned it at dinner. I think you were in the bathroom. Evanora asked me something and—I don’t know, she got under my skin. Like she always does. I blurted it out. I didn’t want to hide it from you, I just hadn’t figured out how to tell you yet.” 

Agatha cuts in, gently, “Okay. But— not to burst your bubble but Rio, Jen told me about the contract. After dinner.”

Rio’s head snaps around, brows furrowed. “What?”

“Yeah, she told me after she ran out of the dining room. Just said it sounded like a big deal and you had signed with that company.”

“No.” Rio shakes her head immediately. “No, I didn’t. That’s what I wanted to talk to you about. I haven’t signed it.”

Agatha blinks. Staring at the road but not seeing it. “You haven’t…”

“No,” Rio says again, more firmly. “It’s sitting in my inbox. I read it. Reread it. Reread it again. But no, I haven’t signed. Not yet.”

Agatha finally turns her head. Her voice is soft, barely a breath. “Why?”

Twenty-Five

Chapter Summary

Rio’s POV

Chapter Notes

hey thx for being patient! and to all the new readers who just found me on twitter welcome ily

See the end of the chapter for more notes

She clears her throat. “I will. It’s not like I’m backing out. I just… haven’t made it official yet.”

Jen quirks an eyebrow. Still watching her. Still too sharp.

“When are you going to tell Agatha?”

———

Rio stills.

Like—body freezing, pulse skidding to a stop. Hands pausing mid-fidget with a button on her shirt. The air in the greenhouse suddenly too warm, too still.

And Rio hates that she says it like it’s so obvious. Like it’s easy.

“Why would I tell Agatha?” she says, sharper than intended.

Jen crosses her arms. Leans her hip against the potting table like she has all the time in the goddamn world. “Why wouldn’t you?”

Rio lets out a breath. Looks away. The light filtering through the glass hurts her eyes all of a sudden. It’s late. The sun’s low. 

“No, Jen. Why would I tell Agatha?”

Jen exhales. Loud. “Jesus, Rio.”

“What?”

“I’ve known this entire time.”

That? That surprises her. Because Jen does not catch onto things very fast. 

Rio knows this because she can get under Jen’s skin very fast with even a simple sarcastic comment.

Jen keeps going. “You left a hickey on her neck. And you stayed with her last night?”

Well.

Fuck. 

She doesn’t even have a response to last night. She saw the look Jen gave her when they stepped out of the car. 

And that hickey? That was from—shit, that was from the spa day. 

Jen knew the entire time. 

Jen’s voice cuts through her panic again. “Agatha already knows I know. So let’s skip the bullshit.”

Rio blinks. Eyes sharp now.

“You need to tell her about the contract,” Jen says.

Rio grips the edge of the table behind her. Tight. She knew this conversation was coming—just didn’t expect it from Jen first. And not now. Not tonight. Not with Agatha still in the house and everything already messy.

“I haven’t even signed it yet,” she mutters.

Jen doesn’t blink. “But you’re going to, right?”

Rio swallows.

She doesn’t have an answer for that.

Not yet.

Alice bursts into the greenhouse like she’s been sprinting. Nearly slams into the door.

“Jen!—oh. Hey, Rio. Jen, I need to talk to you.”

She’s breathless. Like actually out of breath. Rio doesn’t know if she ran or if she’s just that wound up. Either way, it’s enough to make her step back a bit.

“Do I need to leave?” Rio asks, already knowing the answer.

“Yes. Please,” Alice says, already pulling Jen toward the other side of the greenhouse.

Rio nods once. “Okay.”

She turns, halfway to the door when Jen calls after her.

“Talk to Agatha, Rio.”

Rio stops.

“You may be my sister, but she’s my best friend—”

“Hey,” Alice says at the same time, followed by a small smack on Jen’s shoulder. 

“Ow,” Jen whines. “What was that for?”

Alice doesn’t even answer. She just stares at Rio instead. “She’s my best friend, Rio. Talk to her. Please.”

Rio nods again, slower this time. Something pulling at her chest. Heavy. Not bad. Just… thick. Like nerves wrapped in some weird calmness. 

She heads back to the house, careful not to go too fast. Just stays near the front door. Doesn’t hear voices—doesn’t know where Billy and Agatha went off to. Maybe upstairs. Maybe outside. She doesn’t ask.

Just starts walking little laps in the entryway, slow circles like her body needs to move even if her brain’s stalled out. Her nerves are still shot. This house doesn’t help. Too big. Too cold. Too much Evanora baked into the walls.

She’s halfway through a third lap when she hears it.

“Ready to blow this popsicle stand?”

Agatha. Behind her.

Rio turns immediately. Nodding fast enough she’s dizzy. “Let’s get the fuck out of here, please.”

They get in the car and Agatha seems—off.

Not in a cold way. Just quiet. Pulled back into herself like she’s sorting through something she doesn’t want to say out loud yet. Which, fair. Jen knew the whole time. And she clearly didn’t want that.

So Rio keeps it simple. Keeps it safe. She talks to Billy instead, who slides into the backseat and immediately starts rattling off questions about the greenhouse and sunlight. About soil acidity and the best time to repot something. She answers them all, grateful for it. Grateful to have something to fill the silence. 

She’s never had someone so curious about plants before. Not like this. Not a teenager, anyway. And he’s not even doing it in that impress me with your knowledge way adults always expect. He’s just curious. Wants to know how things grow. What makes them bloom. What hurts them. What helps them stay.

It’s nice.

By the time they pull up to Wanda’s apartment, the air inside the car has evened out some. The silence isn’t so sharp. Rio watches Billy unbuckle his seatbelt. She watches Billy ask about what to tell Wanda, Agatha responding and then a wave with a quick goodbye, and he’s heading up the walkway. Agatha watches too, quiet still, hands on the steering wheel like she’s bracing for something.

She doesn’t say anything yet.

And neither does Rio.

But she’s going to. 

Just… needs to grow a pair. 

Then she turns toward Agatha, finally. “Where to next?” she asks, keeping her voice soft. Gentle.

Agatha doesn’t look at her, just shifts into gear and says, “Let’s go back to my place. There’s wine there at least.” She tries to make it sound casual, but Rio hears it—something tucked underneath the ease, trying too hard.

Rio lets out a low laugh anyway, hoping it helps. “Okay, Agatha—” she leans back, lets herself breathe a little, “as you wish.”

The car slips into silence, the kind that feels calm but full. The highway rises ahead of them, dark and steady, headlights cutting through the purple wash of dusk. Rio glances over once—Agatha’s fingers tight on the wheel. Something’s clearly pressing against the edges of her calm.

Rio feels it too. She’s been feeling it since dinner. Since before.

She wants to talk. Say it. Ask. Something. Anything.

And then—both of them at once:

“Can we—”

“I think—”

They stop, blinking at each other, caught in the timing.

Rio gives a little tilt of her head. “Ladies first.”

Agatha exhales a faint smile, quick and tight. “Can we talk?” she asks, barely looking before turning her eyes back to the road.

Rio’s smile drops a little, not in a bad way—just deeper. Steadier. She nods once. “Of course, Agatha. That’s what I was going to ask you too.”

The words feel heavier now, resting between them. Rio watches her, studies the way her jaw tightens even though she’s not reacting otherwise. 

She reaches over. Lets her hand settle on Agatha’s thigh, warm and sure.

Agatha flinches just slightly. Not fear—just startled. Like it pulled her straight out of wherever she’d spiraled.

“Agatha,” Rio says, quieter now.

She turns her head, just enough. Enough for Rio to see the worry swimming in her eyes.

“Yeah?” Agatha says, voice rough around the edges.

Rio pauses. Half a second. Maybe less. Then, “I need to tell you about work. My work.”

Agatha nods once, her throat bobbing with a swallow.

Rio keeps her hand where it is, thumb moving in slow, steady circles. Then she starts.

“It’s about the call I got earlier today,” she says, watching Agatha’s profile carefully. “It’s from a woman named Kate Bishop. She owns or is part of this high-end event planning company in New York. Real deal. She’s been looking for a florist.”

No reaction. Just Agatha breathing in that too-even way, staring out at the roadt.

Rio keeps going.

“The contract’s…” She huffs a quiet laugh. “It’s ridiculous, Agatha. Financial freedom. Straight up. A monthly retainer that would cover everything. Rent. Groceries. I could stop taking bad clients. Stop doing back-to-back parties every weekend just to keep my business above water.”

Her fingers pause, just for a second. Then keep going.

“I could be picky. Finally. Choose the projects I actually care about.”

Still nothing from Agatha. Just that small nod, the kind people give when they’re listening but don’t know what to do with what they’re hearing. Rio doesn’t take it personally. She wouldn’t know what to do either.

“I mentioned it at dinner,” she says. “I think you were in the bathroom. Evanora asked me something and—I don’t know, she got under my skin. Like she always does. I blurted it out. I didn’t want to hide it from you, I just hadn’t figured out how to tell you yet.”

Agatha speaks for the first time in minutes. Quiet. Measured. “Okay. But—not to burst your bubble but Rio, Jen told me about the contract. After dinner.”

Rio’s head snaps around. “What?”

“Yeah, she told me after she ran out of the dining room. Just said it sounded like a big deal and you had signed with that company.”

“No.” Her voice is sharp. Immediate. She shakes her head. “No, I didn’t. That’s what I wanted to talk to you about. I haven’t signed it.”

Agatha blinks. Still staring at the road, but Rio can tell she’s not really seeing it anymore. “You haven’t…”

“No,” Rio says again, firmer this time. “It’s sitting in my inbox. I read it. Reread it. Reread it again. But no, I haven’t signed. Not yet.”

Agatha finally turns her head, and when she speaks, her voice is barely there.

“Why?”

Rio breathes in slowly, watching the road, watching her. She feels the weight of it sitting in her chest, crawling its way up until it reaches her mouth.

“I know we said it would just end at the end of the wedding,” she starts, voice low. Honest. “And if you asked me a week ago why I wouldn’t have signed, I would’ve thought you were crazy. That I was crazy.”

She lets out a faint, almost disbelieving laugh. “The deal is so good, Agatha.”

She sees the way Agatha glances at her again—quick, unsure.

“But?” she asks.

And that’s it. That’s the cue.

Rio turns slightly, enough to really face her, hand still resting on Agatha’s leg, thumb drawing light circles again.

“But,” she says quietly, “Agatha. I don’t do this.”

She gestures between them, the space that’s somehow always full even when they’re not touching.

“I don’t do this. But here I am. With you. Doing it. Whatever this is.”

Her throat feels tight now, the words fighting through. She continues. She has to. 

“I can’t stop thinking about you. About us. What it could maybe turn into.”

She watches Agatha from the side, sees her knuckles whiten slightly against the wheel, but she doesn’t say anything yet.

Rio keeps going.

“I used to hate Westview. Everything about it. Well—almost everything.”

That pulls a small twitch of Agatha’s mouth, but it fades fast.

Rio presses on. “Except Lilia’s—your bookstore. And the garden.”

That part comes out softer. She swallows, her hand curling a bit against Agatha’s thigh.

“I don’t do feelings. I really don’t do kids or teens. I don’t do any of this.”

She looks at her now, straight on.

“And here we are.”

Another pause. Then—

“I can’t stay away. And honestly? I don’t want to.” She breathes, steady and open now, no more holding it in. “So I want to talk to you about what this could mean. For us.”

The words land between them, heavier than anything she’s said all night.

Rio waits.

Watches the way Agatha’s jaw moves like she’s chewing through emotion.

Waits for her to say something—anything. Even no.

Just… not silence.

Agatha makes a turn and Rio feels the force of the car pull her away from Agatha a bit. She returns, rubbing circles still on her thighs. 

The silence on the way into the neighborhood feels louder than anything Rio’s ever heard.

Agatha’s grip is tight on the wheel. Not dangerous—just focused. Like she’s holding something in by force.

Rio doesn’t say a word. She’s said enough. Maybe too much.

Nerves prickle at the back of her neck. Maybe she pushed way too far. Past whatever “this” is. 

The car slows, turns, then finally glides into the driveway. Agatha puts it in park, but doesn’t move right away. Just turns toward her, and Rio sees it—those eyes. Shiny. Not crying, not yet. But close.

“Come on,” Agatha says quietly. “Let’s continue this inside.”

Rio nods, following her out of the car, the silence still thick between them—but not awkward. Just heavy. Full of everything they’ve both said. Everything they haven’t.

Inside, it’s dim and quiet. Familiar. They both move toward the couch like they’ve done it a thousand times, like their bodies already know the way.

They sit—close, but not touching. That space again. Full of things neither of them knows how to say yet.

Agatha sighs softly as she settles, her shoulder barely a breath away from Rio’s.

Then she speaks.

“Rio,” she says, voice low, unsteady, “I don’t—uh—I don’t know what you’re asking from me.”

Rio blinks. Fair. That’s fair.

Because technically, she hadn’t really asked anything.

“I think, uh—” Rio starts, trying to shape the feelings into something solid, something less terrifying. “I think what I’m saying is… I don’t know if I can sign it. Not with whatever we have going.”

Agatha doesn’t react right away, just nods slowly, lips pressing together.

“Okay,” she says, just that.

They sit in it. Long enough she can hear Agatha’s breathing in the quiet of the house. Then Agatha turns to her their shoulders brushing, voice quieter now. Honest in a way that sinks deep into Rio’s core.

“Rio, I’ll be honest. When Jen told me about the contract, I wanted to throw up.”

Rio swallows a lump in her throat. 

“But you telling me about it? How good it is? How hard you’ve worked for this?”

Agatha looks at her then—really looks.

“You need to sign it.”

And that’s what does it. Not yelling. Not anger. Just that. 

You need to sign it. 

Rio feels it—actually feels it. Like her heart is splitting in two. A real crack, deep and sharp and awful.

She looks away, blinking hard. Swallowing the lump climbing up her throat. Because fuck.

This feels like loss.

Loss she hasn’t had since senior year. 

And she’s not even sure they’ve had enough time together to lose anything. But still—she feels it anyway. Because no - 

It’s been enough time. More than enough time. 

It is a loss. 

Rio feels it - like it’s already slipping through her hands.

Agatha’s voice cuts through the silence.

“Look,” she says, and it’s already breaking something open in Rio’s chest. “I, uh—I hate the idea that you’re leaving. Whenever that is.”

Rio swallows, hard.

“But Rio, this is huge. If you’re telling me right now you can’t sign it because of me—” Agatha shakes her head, eyes shining again. “I can’t be the reason for that. You have to take it.”

Before Rio can say anything, Agatha reaches for her hand—gripping it tight, like it hurts to let go.

“I know you’ve been working so hard for so long,” she says. “This would set you up. For a while. I can’t watch you not sign it.”
